Here is the complete, structured answer covering every Go source file in the admission controller pipeline:

---

## API Server Admission Controller Pipeline — Complete File Map

The pipeline has **9 layers**. A request flows: `ApplyTo` assembles the chain → `NewFromPlugins` wraps it as `reinvoker(chainAdmissionHandler)` → on each request, `reinvoker.Admit` runs all mutating plugins serially (with optional reinvocation), then `reinvoker.Validate` runs all validating plugins → `MutatingAdmissionWebhook.Admit` fans out serially to each webhook; `ValidatingAdmissionWebhook.Validate` fans out in parallel.

---

### Layer 1 — Core Framework

| File | Key Symbols | Role |
|------|-------------|------|
| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/interfaces.go` | `Interface`, `MutationInterface`, `ValidationInterface`, `Attributes`, `ObjectInterfaces`, `ReinvocationContext`, `PluginInitializer`, `InitializationValidator`, `ConfigProvider`, `Operation` | **The foundation.** Every interface the pipeline is built on. `MutationInterface.Admit` is called in the mutating phase; `ValidationInterface.Validate` in the validating phase; `ReinvocationContext` tracks whether a second Admit pass is needed. |
| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugins.go` | `Plugins`, `Plugins.Register`, `Plugins.NewFromPlugins`, `Plugins.InitPlugin`, `ValidateInitialization`, `PluginInitializers` | **Registry and chain assembly.** `Register()` stores a `Factory` by name. `NewFromPlugins()` iterates the ordered plugin list, calls `InitPlugin()` for each (which calls `Initialize()` then `ValidateInitialization()`), decorates it, then wraps the slice as `newReinvocationHandler(chainAdmissionHandler(handlers))` — this is where the chain is born. |
| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/chain
... (truncated)
